[Bhс╣Ыgvan╠Дgiras.тАФekatriс╣Е┼Ыatkam. ┼Ы─Бl─Бdevatyam. ─Бnuс╣гс╣нubham: 6. pathy─Бpan╠Дkti; 7. paroс╣гс╣Зih; 15. 3-av. 5-p. ati┼Ыakvar─л; 17. prast─Бrapan╠Дkti; 21. ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti; 25, 31. 3-p. praj─Бpaty─Б bс╣Ыhat─л; 26. s─Бmn─л triс╣гс╣нubh; 27-30. pratiс╣гс╣нh─Бn─Бmag─Бyatr─л; 23-31. 1-av. 3-p.]

Comment

тМКPartly proseтАФ25 to end.тМЛ Found also in P─Бipp. xvi. (in the verse-order 1-3, 5, 4, 6-10, 14, 16, 11, 12, 13, 15, 17, 21, 18, 20, 19, 24, 23, 22, 25-31). The hymn is not noticed in V─Бit.; but several verses (1, 15, 18, 22, 24) are quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 66. 22-30, in connection with an inauguration-ceremony (savayaj├▒a) in which a house (a toy house?) is an object given.

Translations

Translation
  1. Of the props (upam├нt), of the supports (pratim├нt), and also of
    the connectors (? parim├нt) of the dwelling (┼Ы─Б╠Бl─Б) that possesses all
    choice things, we unfasten the tied (naddh├б) [parts].

Griffith

We loose the ties and fastenings of the house that holds all precious things, The bands of pillars and of stays, the ties of beams that form the roof.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What of thee is tied, O thou that possessest all choice things, what
    fetter and knot is made, that with a spell (v─Б╠Бc) I make fall apart, as
    Brihaspati [did] Bala.
Notes

All the mss. read bal├бm (not val├бm) in c, as also Ppp.
(bс╣Ыhaspatiс╣Б vahaс╣Б balam). Our Bp. has in d sraс╣Е┼Ыay─Бmi: tv├бt. The
Anukr. seems to imply the abbreviation of iva to тАЩva in c.

Griffith

All-wealthy House! each knot and band, each cord that is attached to thee I with my spell untie, as erst Brihaspati disclosed the cave.

mss. read m─Б╠Бnasya patni in d; our edition emends to m─Бn-. The
pada-text has ├║ddhit─Б, undivided, in e (as at xviii. 2. 34, and

root dh─Б is not mentioned there, though we find han superfluously
included. Ppp. reads y─Бni te anta┼Ы ciky─Бny ─Бmedho тАШnty─Бya kaс╣Б; and,
for d, sarv─Б m─Бnasya patny─Б.

Griffith

We loose the loops which men have bound within thee, loops to tie and hold. Be gracious, when erected, to our bodies, Lady of the Home.

    [and] seat; seat of the gods art thou, O heavenly dwelling.

Griffith

Store-house of Soma, Agni’s hall, the ladies’ bower, the resi- dence, The seat of Gods art thou, O Goddess House.

Translation
  1. The thousand-eyed net (├бkс╣гu), stretched out as opa┼Ы├б on the
    division-line (viс╣г┼лv├бnt), tied down, put on, do we with worship
    (br├бhman) unfasten.
Notes

Abhihita in c doubtless contains the suggestion of abhidh─Бni ‘a
halter.’ Geldner (Ved. Stud. i. 136) wants to make of akс╣гu a ‘stake’
or ‘pillar.’ Viс╣г┼лvant probably means the ‘parting of the hair, crown’
(so Zimmer), here the ridge of the roof. Ppp. begins with yakс╣гmopi┼Ыam,
and has in c the easier reading apinaddham apihitam.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou coverest within the fire, the men together with the cattle
    (pa┼Ы├║); thou rich in births, rich in progeny, we unfasten thy fetters.
Notes
Griffith

Agni thou shelterest within, and people with domestic beasts. We loose the bonds that fasten thee, mother of multitudes to come!

Whitney
Translation
  1. Between both heaven and earth what expanse [there is], therewith
    do I accept this dwelling of thine; the atmosphere that pervades
    (vim─Б╠Бna) space (r├бjas), that do I make a paunch (ud├бra) for
    treasures; therewith I accept the house for this man.
Notes

This verse in K─Бu┼Ы. 66. 28 accompanies the “acceptance” of the house in
question. The Anukr. calls it an ati┼Ыakvar─л, though it contains only
57 syllables (12 + 12: 11 + 11: 11) instead of 60. Ppp. reads at end of
b t─Бi тАЩm─Бс╣Б (an abbreviation which is here acceptable, as making a
good triс╣гс╣нubhтАФp─Бda тМКsuch was the case at ix. 2. 7 alsoтМЛ), and in e
yac ch─Бl─Бс╣Б for tena ┼Ы-.

Griffith

All space that lies between the earth and heaven, therewith I take this house for thy possession, And all that measures out the air’s mid-region I make a hollow to contain thy treasures. Therewith I take the house for his possession.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Rich in refreshment, rich in milk, fixed (ni-mi), built upon the
    earth, bearing all food, O dwelling, do not thou injure those accepting
    [thee].
Notes
Griffith

Rich in prosperity, rich in milk, founded and built upon the earth, Injure not thy receivers, House who holdest food of every sort!’

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wrapped (─Б-vс╣Ы) with grass, clothing itself in palad├бs, the
    dwelling, place of rest (niv├й┼Ыan─л) of living creatures, like the
    nightтАФbuilt on the earth thou standest, like a she-elephant, having
    feet.
Notes

That is, apparently, heavy and big on the four corner posts, like an
elephant (female because ‘dwelling’ is feminine) on its feet. With b
compare xii. i. 6 b. The verse as a prast─Бrapan╠Дkti (11 + 12: 8 +
8) has no irregularity which the Anukr. is wont to heed.

Griffith

Grass-covered, clad with straw, the house, like Night, gives rest to man and beast. Thou standest, built upon the earth, like a she-elephant, borne on feet.

Whitney
Translation
  1. [The dwelling] which is fixed with two sides, with four sides,
    which with six sidesтАФthe eight-sided, the ten-sided dwelling, the
    mistress of the building, Agni lies in like an embryo.
Notes

The pada-text reads aс╣гс╣н─Бре░pakс╣г─Бm in c, by Pr─Бt. iii. 2; iv. 94.
тМКAs to pakс╣гa, cf. iii. 7. 3.тМЛ The verse is a good pan╠Дkti, involving
only the resolution m─Б╠Бnasi-a in d, but the Anukr. absurdly treats
it as of four p─Бdas; and, in accordance with this, the pada-mss. mark
a p─Бda division after ┼Ы─Б╠Бl─Бm.

Griffith

Within the house constructed with two side-posts, or with four, or six. Built with eight side-posts, or with ten, lies Agni like a babe unborn.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрд╛) рдЬреЛ (рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛) рджреЛ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╡рд╛рд▓реА [рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рдордзреНрдп рдореЗрдВ рдПрдХ, рдФрд░ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдо рдореЗрдВ рдПрдХ-рдПрдХ рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛ], (рдЪрддреБрд╖реНрдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛) рдЪрд╛рд░ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╡рд╛рд▓реА [рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рдордзреНрдп рдореЗрдВ рдПрдХ рдФрд░ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡, рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдо, рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдг рдФрд░ рдЙрддреНрддрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдПрдХ-рдПрдХ рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛ], (рдпрд╛) рдЬреЛ (рд╖рдЯреНрдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛) рдЫрд╣ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╡рд╛рд▓реА [рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рдмреАрдЪ рдореЗрдВ рдмрдбрд╝реА рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдФрд░ рджреЛ-рджреЛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдо рдФрд░ рдПрдХ-рдПрдХ рдЙрддреНрддрд░ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдг рдореЗрдВ рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛрдВ] (рдирд┐рдореАрдпрддреЗ) рдмрдирд╛рдИ рдЬрд╛рддреА рд╣реИред [рдЙрд╕рдХреЛ рдФрд░] (рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдореН) рдЖрда рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╡рд╛рд▓реА [рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рдмреАрдЪ рдореЗрдВ рдПрдХ рдФрд░ рдЪрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдУрд░ рджреЛ-рджреЛ рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛрдВ] рдФрд░ (рджрд╢рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдореН) рджрд╢ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╡рд╛рд▓реА [рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЗ рдордзреНрдп рдореЗрдВ рджреЛ рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдФрд░ рдЪрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рджрд┐рд╢рд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ рджреЛ-рджреЛ рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛрдВ], [рдЙрд╕] (рдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп) рд╕рдореНрдорд╛рди рдХреА (рдкрддреНрдиреАрдореН) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╣рд╛рд░реА (рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛рдореН) рд╢рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдореЗрдВ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдЬрд╛рдард░рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐ рдФрд░ (рдЧрд░реНрднрдГ рдЗрд╡) рдЧрд░реНрднрд╕реНрде рдмрд╛рд▓рдХ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдЖ рд╢рдпреЗ) рдореИрдВ рдард╣рд░рддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБ реереирезрее

Whitney
Translation
  1. I go forward, O dwelling, turned toward thee, uninjuring, that art
    turned toward me; for within [are] fire and waters, the first door of
    right (с╣Ыt├б).
Notes

Ppp. reads at the end prathamobh─Б. The mss. all have ca rt├бsya in
c-d. The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 66. 25, accompanying the action of
‘going forward with (─Бd─Бya) water-pot [and] fire.’

Griffith

Turned to thee, House! I come to thee, innocent, turned to welcome me: For Fire and Water are within, the first chief door of sacrifice.
